<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8c128f7f-3e60-44ad-9e45-490b72d8d5f9'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

  <span id="freeText16995319369883525784" style="display:none"><b>TWO MEN WHO HATE EACH OTHER. ONE IMPOSSIBLE MISSION. A LEGEND IN THE MAKING.</b><br /><br />A warrior with nothing to fight for is paired with a thieving assassin with nothing to lose. Together they must steal a treasure that no one can reach. The Crown Tower is the impregnable remains of the grandest fortress ever built and home to the realm’s most valuable possessions. But it isn’t gold or jewels the old wizard is after, and this prize can only be obtained by the combined talents of two remarkable men. Now if Arcadius can just keep Hadrian and Royce from killing each other, they just might succeed.<br /><br /><i>The Riyria Revelations</i> and <i>The Riyria Chronicles</i> are two separate, but related series, and you can start reading with either <i>Theft of Swords</i> (publication order) or <i>The Crown Tower</i> (chronological order).</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Wow, you are good! I have a spreadsheet that has the ages of the Riyria people at various times. When Royce and Hadrian first met Hadrian is 20 and Ro<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Wow, you are good! I have a spreadsheet that has the ages of the Riyria people at various times. When Royce and Hadrian first met Hadrian is 20 and Royce is 31. At the start of Theft of Swords Hadrian is 31 and Royce is 42. So 11 years between the start of the two series.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

Please keep it up! Can&#39;t wait to read the others. Should i wait to start revalations until all the chronicles are out?</a>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/1598503-michael"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1442493571i/1598503._UX100_CR0,20,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/1598503-michael">Michael</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Revelations is a complete series and all the books of it are out. There are six in total released in three, two-book omnibus volumes: Theft of Swords <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Revelations is a complete series and all the books of it are out. There are six in total released in three, two-book omnibus volumes: Theft of Swords | Rise of Empire | Heir of Novron. <br /><br />As for when "all of Chronicles is out." There is no way to tell when that will be. The way I handle those books is I release a title, then check to see if the "boys" have overstayed their welcome. If it looks like people are starting to tire of them, then I won't put out a next. If people still want more, then I will certainly do another one. In December the third Chronicle came out (The Death of Dulgath) and now that we are about six months out from that release I can say that there probably will be a fourth but I have no idea when I'll write it or when it will come out. The reason is because I have to work Riyria releases around release dates for my new series "The Legends of the First Empire. I've written all six of those books but there will be editing for quite some time to come yet. <br /><br />TL:DR version: No need to wait - you should start reading Revelations now!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_422467010" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/422467010" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1598503-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442493571p2/1598503.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/422467010?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/1598503-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

          marked it as to-read


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span> (Review from the author)


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1598503-michael?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1598503-michael?shelf=the-riyria-chonicles">the-riyria-chonicles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1598503-michael?shelf=sword-play">sword-play</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1598503-michael?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1598503-michael?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1598503-michael?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1598503-michael?shelf=books-i-ve-written">books-i-ve-written</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer422467010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14262283576499065221">If you seen my "reviews" of any of my books, you know I use this space to update people on various aspects of the books such as sales or specials. <br/><br/><b>Update 7/29/19</b>: ON SALE for just <a href='https://adbl.co/2NkrRZZ' rel='nofollow noopener'>$5.00 on Audible.com</a> Now until August 4th. That's a savings of 82% so if you listen to audioboooks, now would be a great time to start into the Riyria Chronicle series!<br/><br/><b>Update 5/23/18</b>: This book (along with 8 other epic fantasies from the likes of Brandon Sanderson, Naomi Novik, Robin Hobb, and others) has been selected</span>
  <span id="freeText14262283576499065221" style="display:none">If you seen my "reviews" of any of my books, you know I use this space to update people on various aspects of the books such as sales or specials. <br><br><b>Update 7/29/19</b>: ON SALE for just <a href="https://adbl.co/2NkrRZZ" rel="nofollow noopener">$5.00 on Audible.com</a> Now until August 4th. That's a savings of 82% so if you listen to audioboooks, now would be a great time to start into the Riyria Chronicle series!<br><br><b>Update 5/23/18</b>: This book (along with 8 other epic fantasies from the likes of Brandon Sanderson, Naomi Novik, Robin Hobb, and others) has been selected for <a href="https://adbl.co/2Ln9qCM" rel="nofollow noopener">Audible's Summer Listen 2-for-1 Sale</a>. Since it's the first in the series, this is an excellent time to dive into the series that takes place 10 years before the events of the Riyria Revelations. Here are the other books on sale:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1527090805i/25585762.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But you have to hurry, the sale ends May 24 at 11:59 PM PDT.<br><br><b>Update 12/05/17: </b>The fourth Riyria Chronicle (The Disappearance of Winter's Daughter) is "soft released" today. What is a "soft release"? Well it means you can get the book by buying directly from me, but the books won't be in the retail stores until after the Age of War release (due to a non-compete clause in my current contract. So, if you want more adventures with Royce and Hadrian, you're in luck!<br><br><b>Update 09/26/12: </b> When I finished <i>The Riyria Revlations</i> I secretly hoped that they would be successful enough so that I could write more stories with two of my favorite characters: Royce and Hadrian. The books have been out for less than a year, but already it looks like a big success. By my calculations the series has sold more than 200,000 copies (including the self-published versions). <br><br>I'm being very careful about additional works related to the world of Elan. I don't want to overstay my welcome. We all know television series, or book series, that stayed around long past their time, and it is a sad thing indeed. I won't let that happen to anything that I create.<br><br>But, feedback has that people want more Royce and Hadrian, and as I love writing them (and my wife constantly bugged me) I was more than happy to write more...as long as I still had compelling stories and could pen a riveting tale.<br><br>I think I've accomplished this in the next installment. This book, and the series, actually go back in time and explore the founding of Team Riyria. For those who have read the last installment of The Riyria Revelations (Heir of Novron) you'll know I setup my dominoes in a very careful way, and I liked watching everything fall into place. I didn't want to risk ruining that by "tacking" on to what was designed to end as it has. I'm not saying I won't one day write books "on into the future" after the final revelations...a lot will depend on the readers, and whether they want to see more. Again I'm going to be cautious and plan to "quit while I'm ahead" rather than dragging it out and have people disappointed.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1612033472" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1612033472" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1612033472?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Brandon Sanderson and Bromances</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=book-boyfriend-material">book-boyfriend-material</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=bro-mantic">bro-mantic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1612033472" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16186085775983224614"><b>Sale Alert: This is the kindle daily deal 21Mar20 for <a href='https://www.amazon.com/dp/B00A2D7VCA/ref=s9_acsd_al_bw_c2_x_19_i?pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&pf_rd_s=merchandised-search-2&pf_rd_r=N3X5N5FCQESR01DNHPM1&pf_rd_t=101&pf_rd_p=e95b8710-6d62-4cf7-8fee-23f36a9fb4dc&pf_rd_i=11552285011' rel='nofollow noopener'>$2.99</a> <br/><br/>Read with some of the fantasy buffs at <a>Buddies Books & Baubles</a><br/><br/>I was a little worried to read this prequel. I totally <b>LoVeD </b>Hadrian and Royce in the Riyria Revelations and it is a completed series. Did I really want to go back to their beginnings to see how it all started??? And the answer is….<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419945804ra/13149605.gif' width='400' height='478' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>MJS <b>is not</b> that author who couldn’t figure out what to write next and so decided hey I’ll write more books in the same world because $$$. Nope not</b></span>
  <span id="freeText16186085775983224614" style="display:none"><b>Sale Alert: This is the kindle daily deal 21Mar20 for <a href="https://www.amazon.com/dp/B00A2D7VCA/ref=s9_acsd_al_bw_c2_x_19_i?pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&amp;pf_rd_s=merchandised-search-2&amp;pf_rd_r=N3X5N5FCQESR01DNHPM1&amp;pf_rd_t=101&amp;pf_rd_p=e95b8710-6d62-4cf7-8fee-23f36a9fb4dc&amp;pf_rd_i=11552285011" rel="nofollow noopener">$2.99</a> <br><br>Read with some of the fantasy buffs at <a>Buddies Books &amp; Baubles</a><br><br>I was a little worried to read this prequel. I totally <b>LoVeD </b>Hadrian and Royce in the Riyria Revelations and it is a completed series. Did I really want to go back to their beginnings to see how it all started??? And the answer is….<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419945804ra/13149605.gif" width="400" height="478" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>MJS <b>is not</b> that author who couldn’t figure out what to write next and so decided hey I’ll write more books in the same world because $$$. Nope not at all, <b>he wrote it because his wife fell in love with another man.</b><br><blockquote>
<i>It’s the classic story of a husband whose wife falls for another man—a more dashing and charming gent. <b>It sounds tragic, but this tale is a bit different because the love affair is between a real woman and a fictional man.</b> My wife—let’s call her Robin (because that’s her name)—has developed an infatuation for Hadrian Blackwater. I’m not sure how I feel about enabling my wife’s relationship with another man, but at least I know this guy is trustworthy</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464817471ra/19280674.gif" width="400" height="286" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote>
<br>As soon as I read that in the dedication I KNEW that MJS was not just pumping out more books for the sake of $$$ but definitely for the love of the world, the characters and his wife. After that I just relaxed and had a great time with it.<br><br><b>Can you read this first???</b> <br><br>Yes, there aren’t any spoilers for the future series. BUT….that said I will say that I really liked catching the little hints and cameos of characters that we get to know better later on. My personal recommendation is to read The Riyria Revelations first and then move on to these.<br><br><b>But won’t I be a little bored since I already kind of know what happens from Riyria Revelations?</b><br><br>I was also a little worried about that. The answer is a resounding NO…you will not be bored at all. There are so many great things in this. One of the first things I was really excited about is that we get a Gwen PoV and it is fantastic. <br><blockquote><i> Why did we leave Calis? Why did you give me a northern name? And most importantly, Why does it mean so much to you for us to go to this mythical place called Medford? Stubbornly her mother had refused to answer, except to say that God had told her to go. When Gwen asked which god, her mother had replied, “The one who walks as a man.”</i></blockquote>
<br>The second thing is that Royce and Hadrian are just starting out and you can see how completely different they are from each other. Hadrian is pretty naive and trusting…while Royce well he was raised by wolves so trust isn’t something he understands at all.<br><blockquote><i>“You have any friends?”<br>“One.”<br>“Arcadius?”<br>“No.”<br>“Where is this friend?”<br>“No idea.”<br>“When was the last time you saw him?”<br>“When he framed me for murder and sent me to prison.”<br>“I don’t think you understand the meaning of the word friend.”<br>“And I think you live in a fairy-tale world where words have consistent meanings…”</i></blockquote>
<br>I really enjoyed this getting to know each other part of their relationship. You can see the threads of the bromance that it will become but you can also see the rocky road they will travel to get there.<br><br>This story went so fast for me and I couldn’t wait to get to some of the moments I knew had to be coming because of the snippets we were told in Riyria Revelations.<br><br>As MJS said he could write one book covering a year in Harian and Royce’s life leading up to Riyria Revelations which is 12 books. You know what…. <b>I WOULD READ THEM ALL</b> if they are even close to as good as this one.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16186085775983224614" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=assassins">assassins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fae">fae</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1222010126" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer526535176997059476"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You realize I'm just taking you to die?” <br/>“I hope to disappoint you.” <br/>“You won't.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Thankfully Hadrian did disappoint Royce, and thus Riyria was born. After a long and hectic week, getting back to Elan and reading the first adventure of my beloved pair of thieves was like <b>coming home</b>. Thank you Mr.Sullivan for giving us <i>another</i> <b>high fantasy mastepiece</b>!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399304146ra/9532055.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Excuse me. My name is Hadrian Blackwater.”<br/>“Congratulations.”<br/>“Um... what's yours?”<br/>“Leave me alone.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16043804.The_Crown_Tower__The_Riyria_Chronicles___1_' title='The Crown Tower (The Riyria Chronicles, #1) by Michael J. Sullivan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Crown Tower</a> offered u</span>
  <span id="freeText526535176997059476" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You realize I'm just taking you to die?” <br>“I hope to disappoint you.” <br>“You won't.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Thankfully Hadrian did disappoint Royce, and thus Riyria was born. After a long and hectic week, getting back to Elan and reading the first adventure of my beloved pair of thieves was like <b>coming home</b>. Thank you Mr.Sullivan for giving us <i>another</i> <b>high fantasy mastepiece</b>!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399304146ra/9532055.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Excuse me. My name is Hadrian Blackwater.”<br>“Congratulations.”<br>“Um... what's yours?”<br>“Leave me alone.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16043804.The_Crown_Tower__The_Riyria_Chronicles___1_" title="The Crown Tower (The Riyria Chronicles, #1) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crown Tower</a> offered us a great insight into the beginning of Royce and Hadrian's partnership and friendship when Arcadius paired them to steal a treasure from the Crown Tower. Meanwhile, Gwen stepped towards her freedom and shaped her future to her own liking, waiting for <i>him</i>, the one she was bound to help and save in more than one ways. I expected <b>adventure</b> and <b>swordfights</b> and <b>assassinations</b> and <b>banters</b> and <b>twists and turns</b> like only <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2063919.Michael_J__Sullivan" title="Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">Michael J. Sullivan</a> can write, and I got them all. I inhaled every page, I <b>laughed</b> and yelled with <b>excitement</b> and <b>loved</b> deeply, but there was <i>more</i>. Mr.Sullivan gave us more. He gave us the story of a girl who was tired of being disrespected and humiliated and manhandled, the story of a young man who gave up killing and sought a greater purpose in his life, the story of another young man who was raised by wolves and didn't hesitate to kill his problems because no one ever showed him there is another way. <b>I witnessed the forge of heroes</b>, <i>my</i> heroes, and my heart swelled with pride and love and awe.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I believe there's a human inside that cloak, Hadrian. You just have to find a way to break through to it.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>One of the many things I admire in Mr.Sullivan's writing is his ability to create <b>three dimensional characters</b>, whether they're the protagonists or the helpful farmer or the savage brute. You can feel the difference between Royce and Hadrian of the past and Royce and Hadrian of the present (the Royce of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10790290.Theft_of_Swords__The_Riyria_Revelations___1_" title="Theft of Swords (The Riyria Revelations, #1) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">Theft of Swords</a> is a charming and pleasant fellow compared to his old self), you can see that naive and optimistic and trusting to a fault Hadrian needs Royce to survive in a cruel world, and ruthless Royce needs Hadrian to find goodness in mankind. They're the complete opposites and they had a rocky start, but what's a better way to start a friendship than stabbing a student and murdering five people? (well obviously there is a better way but that's Royce we're talking about). Mr.Sullivan didn't hold back, he showed us their ugly sides without restraint, he made us understand and sympathize with them. And there was also Gwen. Her character is a constant surprise and I was so happy to learn more about her. After all the horrors she went through, she remained kind and caring and helpful, and I cannot think of a better person to shed light into Royce's life, to mold him into a better version of himself. She's become one of my favorite female characters!<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“While she called all of them ladies, Rose knew the only real lady in Medford House was Gwen DeLancy.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Whether you're already a Riyria fan or not, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16043804.The_Crown_Tower__The_Riyria_Chronicles___1_" title="The Crown Tower (The Riyria Chronicles, #1) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crown Tower</a> is the perfect opportunity to dive into a <b>world of pure adventure and absolutely amazing characters</b> and I can assure you,you will enjoy every single moment!</span>
  <a data-text-id="526535176997059476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1529656460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3010634066134550445">''The Riyria Revelations'' is my favorite series and reading it I always wondered how did Royce and Hadrian met so I was very excited to read this book.<br/><br/>In my experience prequels aren't usually done right and they somewhat diminish that awesome feeling you got from the original so I was hoping this would be a good origin story and I'm glad it delivered. <br/><br/>This book made me love Royce and Hadrian even more, I loved how they hated each other when they met because as a result their conversations, or m</span>
  <span id="freeText3010634066134550445" style="display:none">''The Riyria Revelations'' is my favorite series and reading it I always wondered how did Royce and Hadrian met so I was very excited to read this book.<br /><br />In my experience prequels aren't usually done right and they somewhat diminish that awesome feeling you got from the original so I was hoping this would be a good origin story and I'm glad it delivered. <br /><br />This book made me love Royce and Hadrian even more, I loved how they hated each other when they met because as a result their conversations, or more accurately, their bickering was hilarious. Another reason why their initial animosity was so fun for me is because my best friend and me were the same when we first met.<br /><br />The story mostly follows Hadrian through his POV and it was a bit slow paced until he reached Sheridan and had a meeting with Arcadius. I won't give away any spoilers but I'l just say that from that moment everything was just pure fun.<br /><br />Another character from Revelations that got more ''screen time'' was Gwen. Through her chapters we follow her rise from the bottom and we find out how she became The Lady of the House Medford. Those chapters were a bit dark and gruesome but I enjoyed them nevertheless. Gwen is an excellent example of a strong female character.<br /><br />I would have loved to read more about Royce and his adventures with the Black Diamond and his time in the Manzant prison but I was very much satisfied with his part in this story.<br /><br />I loved the ending of this book and the way everything fit together and I can't wait to read the next one.</span>

<div id="review_1349766238" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1349766238" />
    <a title="Jody " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41767362-jody"><img alt="Jody " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558120407p2/41767362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1349766238?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jody " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jody " href="/user/show/41767362-jody">Jody </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41767362-jody?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1349766238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13367013732342171523"><b>All the stars *****</b><br/><br/>Royce and Hadrian are my favorite duo in the fantasy world. I say this without any trace of doubt at all. MJS could write 30 books about these two unlikely Heroes and I would happily devour them with glee. And after reading <i>The Crown Tower</i>, this installment will take it's rightful place on my favorites shelf.<br/><br/>Michael J. Sullivan has a way of telling a story that just really connects with me. He doesn't make it complicated or try to do anything that hasn't been done before, but </span>
  <span id="freeText13367013732342171523" style="display:none"><b>All the stars *****</b><br /><br />Royce and Hadrian are my favorite duo in the fantasy world. I say this without any trace of doubt at all. MJS could write 30 books about these two unlikely Heroes and I would happily devour them with glee. And after reading <i>The Crown Tower</i>, this installment will take it's rightful place on my favorites shelf.<br /><br />Michael J. Sullivan has a way of telling a story that just really connects with me. He doesn't make it complicated or try to do anything that hasn't been done before, but I can just relate with his characters and writing style. I feel like if I come home from a bad day at work, I can open up a Riyria book and everything just floats away. Yes! That kind of feeling. Not many authors do that for me, but MJS certainly does.<br /><br /><i>The Crown Tower</i> tells the story of how the Riyria duo came to be. The event this book is named after is spoken of several time in the Riyria Revelations books, but that is nothing compared to reading the actual tale. <br /><br />While this book was definitely more about Hadrian than Royce, I was, at first, a little surprised that Gwen got so much page time. Her story arc was just as good as Hadrians and maybe even more important to the overall outcome. She made it complete and really brought it all full circle.<br /><br />There are parts in the Revelations series that refer to when Royce and Hadrian first teamed up, but to read about it was entertaining and bittersweet knowing how they end up. The guys really are opposites and view the world completely different. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"You were right about the swords," Royce said. "You really do need three."<br />"You sound drunk."<br />"I feel drunk - and I hate being drunk. Nothing works the way it's supposed to. And it makes me act stupid....like you."<br />"You're aware I'm in the process of trying to save your life, right?"<br />"What part of stupid don't you understand?"</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />I can't rave about the Riyria books or Michael J. Sullivan's writing enough, but I will stop here and just say simply READ THEM. You won't be disappointed. MJS is an awesome storyteller. I myself am moving on to <i>The Rose and The Thorne</i> immediately. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13367013732342171523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1351979112" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1351979112" />
    <a title="Tammie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3506989-tammie"><img alt="Tammie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604938056p2/3506989.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1351979112?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tammie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tammie" href="/user/show/3506989-tammie">Tammie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17278262-the-crown-tower">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=owned-kindle">owned-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=adult-fantasy">adult-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=owned-paper-back">owned-paper-back</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1351979112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7726995052950120690"><b> TWO MEN WHO HATE EACH OTHER. ONE IMPOSSIBLE MISSION. A LEGEND IN THE MAKING. </b><br/><br/>If you read the Riyria Revelations and wondered how Royce and Hadrian met, then The Crown Tower is the book to read. They are an unlikely pair in many ways and never would have partnered up if not for the wizard Arcadius, who sets them on a quest to steal a book from the Crown Tower, which no one has ever broken into.<br/><br/>It takes a while to get to this point in the book. First we follow Hadrian on his journey to the univer</span>
  <span id="freeText7726995052950120690" style="display:none"><b> TWO MEN WHO HATE EACH OTHER. ONE IMPOSSIBLE MISSION. A LEGEND IN THE MAKING. </b><br /><br />If you read the Riyria Revelations and wondered how Royce and Hadrian met, then The Crown Tower is the book to read. They are an unlikely pair in many ways and never would have partnered up if not for the wizard Arcadius, who sets them on a quest to steal a book from the Crown Tower, which no one has ever broken into.<br /><br />It takes a while to get to this point in the book. First we follow Hadrian on his journey to the university to meet with Arcadius and there is a whole mystery there to solve involving the passengers on a barge and a mysterious man in a dark cloak. This is alternated with chapters about Gwen and her origin story. While I was eager to see how Royce and Hadrian would eventually team up, I still very much enjoyed this part of the book.<br /><br />Eventually Hadrian makes it to the university and meets with Arcadius and officially meets Royce for the first time. The fact that they hate each other from the beginning makes the task of getting them to team up for the tower job more than difficult, but Arcadius sees something in each of them that he knows will make them great assets to each other. This is where the story really takes off. <br /><br />We still get Gwen's story throughout the rest of the book as well. I always liked Gwen in the Revelations series, but now that I've read some chapters in her point of view, I like her even more. There wasn't much action in her chapters, but they were filled with tension even though I knew how things would end up for her.<br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed reading this prequel to The Riyria Revelations. It was fun revisiting Royce and Hadrian and finding out how it all started. My only complaint is that this ended all too soon! I will definitely be reading The Rose and the Thorn.<br /><br />Review also posted at <a href="https://writingsofareader.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Writings of a Reader</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7726995052950120690" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1945381668?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Orient" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Orient" href="/user/show/43587353-orient">Orient</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everybody</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=psychological">psychological</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=hero">hero</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1945381668" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14172831244749791619">A great BR with amazing GR dwellers, <b>Craig</b> and <b>Alex</b> :)<br/><br/><i>
  <b>"All I wanted was to live—I’d forgotten everything else. A clod of dirt doesn’t have dreams. A bit of broken stone doesn’t understand hope. Each morning, all I wanted was to see the next dawn. But you changed that."</b>
</i><br/><br/>When I finished Riyria Revelations, I was so eager to meet the characters again and dived into Riyria Chronicles with pleasure :) If you have, like me, read Michael J. Sullivan’s Riyria Revelations series already, you’ll know t</span>
  <span id="freeText14172831244749791619" style="display:none">A great BR with amazing GR dwellers, <b>Craig</b> and <b>Alex</b> :)<br><br><i>
  <b>"All I wanted was to live—I’d forgotten everything else. A clod of dirt doesn’t have dreams. A bit of broken stone doesn’t understand hope. Each morning, all I wanted was to see the next dawn. But you changed that."</b>
</i><br><br>When I finished Riyria Revelations, I was so eager to meet the characters again and dived into Riyria Chronicles with pleasure :) If you have, like me, read Michael J. Sullivan’s Riyria Revelations series already, you’ll know that Hadrian and Royce, the great partners, weren’t always the perfect team we met and liked. Now at last, in the “Crown Tower” I got an opportunity to know all the nuances in the backstory of the great Riyria. “The Crown Tower” starts The Riyria Chronicles in a compelling way.<br><br>For the new readers, this book will be a great fantasy read, with adventures, engaging action and fights, great presentation of two main male characters and one amazing female in the lead. For the Riyria old-timers this will be a thrilling chance to dive into Hadrian and Royce’s first ever job as partners and of course this book will show how these two quite different men became a great team. <br><br>Characters: What I loved the most is that this book is concentrated not only upon Hadrian and Royce, but also Gwen, who, after this book, is worth my fascination as a strong female character and great personality. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490906432i/22357286.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Of course, I met these characters before, but in Revelations they weren’t so fully fleshed out as I felt they were in “Crown Tower”. As in previous books, Hadrian’s and Royce’s interaction is great, funny and enjoyable to read, adding more fun that it’s only the beginning of their bromance. <br><br><i>
  <b>“My name is Hadrian Blackwater.”<br>“Congratulations.” The reply was as cold as the wind that carried it.<br>“Uh … what’s yours?”<br>The man turned away. “Leave me alone.”</b>
</i><br><br>The first shock that I experienced while reading this book is that there’s a clear difference between Royce and Hadrian that we meet here and in Revelations– in “The Crown Tower” they’re young and more inexperienced. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Lol, just reading the first chapter I found out that Hadrian can be easily robbed as he just got off a ship and despite having traveled a lot, fought in a lot of armies, he resembles a simple unexperienced guy, who just starts his life. Royce is a lot different than Hadrian, so untrusting, grim, always suspecting something. The exact opposite of Hadrian, as Hadrian is a really friendly soul. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> So it was really interesting and great watching the development of their characters.<br><br>This book allowed me to have a closer and more interesting look into the characters, I’ve met in Revelations and knowing exactly how they’re going to develop as the series goes on, spoils matters a bit. I knew what will be the end for them, who’ll make it and who’ll not, which of course leaves the taste of predictability. <br><br>Oh and I just loved the scene with Golden guards!<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490906726ra/22357374.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Narrative: The exact thing I adored in this book is that it continues to be easy, fun, action-filled, straightforward adventurous fantasy story. I can compare this book to a missing part, which fits into Revelations not being boring, repetitive or unimportant. I just felt that “The Crown Tower” has an intriguing plan in his mind, so I must prepare myself for great adventures as everything happens for a reason and so far my playdate in Riyria Chronicles is smooth and logical. Which is why I’m happy that Sullivan presents the unfamiliar parts to Riyria Revelations in unpredictable and engaging way. <br><br>To sum up, I can say that Sullivan once more shines with his skill at creating a page-turner again. Oh and what was a great relief for me: this story doesn’t reach even 400 pages so it’s an easy and light read, especially after my Malazan adventure :D</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <a title="Terence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23206148-terence"><img alt="Terence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473945175p2/23206148.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2184028816?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terence" href="/user/show/23206148-terence">Terence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2184028816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15392164514170648133">Some unexpected things are happening and a university professor appears to be behind them all. Professor Arcadius has brought together a fighter without equal and an incredibly skilled thief. The two are polar opposites and hate one another, but Arcadius has managed to convince them to do one job for him. To steal a single book from a seemingly impregnable fortress.<br/><br/>The Crown Tower could easily have been titled how Hadrian met Royce. Michael J. Sullivan made a good point in saying that Hadrian an</span>
  <span id="freeText15392164514170648133" style="display:none">Some unexpected things are happening and a university professor appears to be behind them all. Professor Arcadius has brought together a fighter without equal and an incredibly skilled thief. The two are polar opposites and hate one another, but Arcadius has managed to convince them to do one job for him. To steal a single book from a seemingly impregnable fortress.<br /><br />The Crown Tower could easily have been titled how Hadrian met Royce. Michael J. Sullivan made a good point in saying that Hadrian and Royce wouldn't have been an instant success as a team because of their differences. It's amazing neither tried to kill the other one. For anyone who has read Riyria Revelations suffice to say Hadrian is even more of an optimist while Royce is far more pessimistic.<br /><br />The story is told largely from three perspectives. Two of these perspectives are obvious as they come from Royce and Hadrian. The third, for me at least, was unexpected. The third perspective came from Gwen. I have to admit I rarely gave Gwen much thought despite her unique position and abilities in Riyria Revelations. I also have to admit, I wouldn't have cared in the least to see her storyline almost completely abandoned. There were at most two or three things about her I was curious about and those simply didn't warrant the number of pages spent detailing her rise from prostitute to lady of her own house.<br /><br />The Crown Tower was good, but didn't quite hit the spot for me. I did find myself feeling the old Riyria magic towards the end of the book though.</span>

<div id="review_967238671" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/967238671" />
    <a title="Conor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30552336-conor"><img alt="Conor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400278909p2/30552336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/967238671?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Conor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Conor" href="/user/show/30552336-conor">Conor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer967238671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9962797154185053995">This was a really fun read with an interesting, fast-paced plot and a number of likeable characters. The story was made more enjoyable by the fact that I was already invested in the 2 main characters from the main Riyria series however I actually think this book might be a better entry point in light of the fact that it does a better job of establishing Royce and Hadrian as distinct characters although the story is only tangentially related to the main plot of the series with the focus of this o</span>
  <span id="freeText9962797154185053995" style="display:none">This was a really fun read with an interesting, fast-paced plot and a number of likeable characters. The story was made more enjoyable by the fact that I was already invested in the 2 main characters from the main Riyria series however I actually think this book might be a better entry point in light of the fact that it does a better job of establishing Royce and Hadrian as distinct characters although the story is only tangentially related to the main plot of the series with the focus of this one being establishing Royce and Hadrian and developing them from 2 lads who are fundamentally opposed to one another (the ruthless assassin vs the honourable warrior) into an effective partnership. Just realized that last sentence was long as fuck but I'm not going to change it now.<br /><br />This prequel did a masterful job of establishing Hadrian and Royce, imo far better than was done in the first few novels of the main series. I especially appreciated how Royce's ruthlessness was made very apparent whereas in the main series early on he seems like his bark is far worse than his bite. This prequel also did a really nice job of establishing Hadrian as a Rambo style deadly killing machine who is disillusioned with a life of violence (although he hasn't throat ripped anyway. yet.). Their clash of personalities and their burgeoning respect and trust is heart of this story (and this is indeed mirrored nicely in the plot as Arcadius hints that the only reason he set them on this mission was so that they would have to learn to work together).<br /><br />We also got Gwen's origin story in this one. While it fleshed out the world a bit and further developed a pretty cool character from the main series in Gwen, I found it to be pretty dull as there wasn't a lot of action going on, we knew how it would end from the main series and it didn't really provide any new information that was relevant to the rest of the series.<br /><br />The plot itself was fun and fast-paced, if a little simple and predictable, likely owing to the focus on the characters. Probably the highlight of the plot was the boat journey early on which had a cool "whodunnit" bit to it as well as some exposition on Hadrian's character. I liked the twist ending, it was unexpected and well-done although it felt a bit abrupt. A lot of Lawrence's killing off of characters has that feeling to it which makes his books all the more suspenseful and unpredictable. I kind of wish we had gotten Royce's POV on the boat incident though, especially as it would have fleshed it out nicely. The ending to the story was also pretty cool with a desperate escape and epic last stand that reminded me of "Butch Cassidy and the Sundance kid" (the cool one from the 60's not the shitty one with Keanu Reeves).</span>
  <a data-text-id="9962797154185053995" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_689840967" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/689840967" />
    <a title="Bookwraiths" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths"><img alt="Bookwraiths" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353765210p2/14716035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/689840967?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookwraiths" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookwraiths" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths">Bookwraiths</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer689840967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer489194291844524852">Originally published at <a href='http://bookwraiths.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bookwraiths Reviews</a><br/><br/><b>THE BUTCH CASSIDAY AND SUNDANCE KID OF FANTASY!</b><br/><br/>For all of you familiar with the Riyria Revelations books, Hadrian Blackwater and Royce Melborn are the Dynamic Duo of fantasy: Hadrian the great warrior with three swords for any occasion and Royce the dark, mysterious assassin waiting to put a dagger in you. Two partners who are as polarly opposite in their personality and outlook on life as in their styles of fighting. No matter their differences however</span>
  <span id="freeText489194291844524852" style="display:none">Originally published at <a href="http://bookwraiths.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookwraiths Reviews</a><br /><br /><b>THE BUTCH CASSIDAY AND SUNDANCE KID OF FANTASY!</b><br /><br />For all of you familiar with the Riyria Revelations books, Hadrian Blackwater and Royce Melborn are the Dynamic Duo of fantasy: Hadrian the great warrior with three swords for any occasion and Royce the dark, mysterious assassin waiting to put a dagger in you. Two partners who are as polarly opposite in their personality and outlook on life as in their styles of fighting. No matter their differences however, these two night and day characters are the most dedicated of partners and friends. <br /><br />But how could they have ever gotten past these issues to form a partnership called Riyria?<br /><br />This is the story Michael J. Sullivan sets out to tell in <i> The Crown Tower</i>, and he accomplishes it with a flair long time readers have come to expect from him. The tale he pens is one of those very rare prequels: a stand alone story which - while tipping its hat so subtly to the older novels - never fails to understand it is a story unto itself. Indeed, Hadrian, Royce and Gwen grabbed the readers attention from the first, drawing them along involuntarily in the turbulence of their story as all three are inevitably drawn together.<br /><br />Naturally, our story takes place before the events of <i>The Theft of Swords</i>, which is the first set of books set in the world of Riyria. Here, Hadrian Blackwater is a young man, still holding onto his youthful naivety yet having seen and done bloody deeds that even he refuses to recall. Our youthful optimist has wandered over half the world since he left his father’s blacksmith shop as a youth, eager to find glory and a worthy cause that his unvanquishable sword skills could be used for. Yet, none of the glory or gold satisfied Hadrian: they made him feel hollow inside actually. So when word reaches him about his father back home, something breaks within him, and he finds himself drawn back to his roots, hoping to find some epiphany about his future. Perhaps some sign as to where or what he should do with the remainder of his life - and with his only skill: killing people. <br /><br />That is where Royce comes in. I cannot tell you how these two meet without giving away spoilers and ruining the surprise, but suffice it to say that Mr. Sullivan crafts this in the perfect way. A set up which not only enlivens what had been a slow story to that point, but also forces our Dynamic Duo to interact with one another for all our entertainment. <br /><br />Naturally, afer meeting and attempting to clear up their differences, Hadrian and Royce find themselves drawn together whether they like it or not. Their mutual goal to plan and conduct a heist that is so impossible that no one has ever tried it! And that is absolutely insane for two strangers such as them to attempt - especially since they absolutely despise one another! <br /><br />I know the fact Hadrian and Royce hate one another came as no surprise to anyone right?<br /><br />Who did not see that coming? <br /><br />These two are oil and water, even in the later books when they have been partners for years, so most certainly they would not enjoy each others company at first meeting. But Mr. Sullivan does something wonderful in this book: he actually takes the time to explain why each of them behave and believe as they do. He then forces each character to confront those same facts about the other and work through their revulsion of the others’ life view. This sets up interesting and hilarious scenes where Royce and Hadrian are bickering, insulting and threatening to murder one another. They argue about everything, even when death is knocking at their door, and each constantly wonders how someone as idiotic as the other person could have survived so long without someone killing them. They are the only duo since Butch Cassidy and the Sundance Kid I have ever seen carry this type of quarreling and cooperation relationship so far and make this entertaining. (Butch Cassidy and the Sundance Kid is a great, classic western for those who don’t know. Go rent it today and understand what I mean!) <br /><br />And we cannot forget Gwen, the mysterious brothel owner, who gradually plays a bigger and bigger role in Revelations. Here we get to understand her life up until she met Hadrian and Royce, how she became a prostitute, and the role she played in Hadrian and Royce actually becoming Riyria. While I can’t say Gwen’s story broke new ground in storytelling, it was well written, eye-opening, and added another layer to this elegant lady who always brightened the pages with her appearance in Revelations. For those reasons, it was a very enjoyable part of the overall prequel.<br /><br />As long time readers already know, Mr. Sullivan has that innate ability to create a page-turner, and <i>The Crown Tower</i> is no different. It is a great read for those who have experienced the wonderful Riyria Revelations and those who have not. The novel has it all: excitement, hilarity, mystery, fighting, and romance. What else could anyone ask for out of a fantasy novel? Nothing. So just go buy the book already, you know you want to.<br /><br /><b>I received this book as an ARC from Netgalley in return for an honest review. The review you have read is my opinion, and mine alone.</b> <br /><br />Royce and Hadrian have not visited me and attempted to bribe or beaten me into writing this. And if they had, I doubt I could really mention it so . . .forget I said anything. *Whispers* Royce hears everything.</span>
  <a data-text-id="489194291844524852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1285804882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1285804882" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1285804882?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18372099-the-crown-tower">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=dr-reading-challenge">dr-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=physical-owned">physical-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1285804882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9847613479865052298"><b>
  <i>"Old lunatic was right...We did make a good team."</i>
</b><br/><br/>And thus a legend was born! I love origins stories of beloved characters and having read the Riyria Revelations first enabled me to have a greater appreciation of the two foremost and main characters, Hadrian and Royce. While one can start their introduction into the world of Riyria through the first Chronicles book, I find that having hindsight in this case really does, oddly, elevate the reading experience. It's awesome being able to pick o</span>
  <span id="freeText9847613479865052298" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"Old lunatic was right...We did make a good team."</i>
</b><br /><br />And thus a legend was born! I love origins stories of beloved characters and having read the Riyria Revelations first enabled me to have a greater appreciation of the two foremost and main characters, Hadrian and Royce. While one can start their introduction into the world of Riyria through the first Chronicles book, I find that having hindsight in this case really does, oddly, elevate the reading experience. It's awesome being able to pick out seemingly throwaway phrases which make one who finished Revelations nod knowingly with a smile, or even smirk, sometimes. A prequel done right, this was an absolutely enjoyable read touching on the main characters on a highly personal level.<br /><br />Even at risk of sounding like a broken record, I'll still say it again... who doesn't want more of Hadrian and Royce? Especially when narrated by the voice of Riyria - Tim Gerard Reynolds. <br /><br /><b>May 2016: Reread with my awesome buddies at BB&amp;B.</b><br /><br />----------------------------------<br /><b>May 2015:</b> Hadrian Blackwater, a noble and idealistic mercenary soldier. Royce Melborn, a dangerous and cynical thief. With such polar opposite personalities, you know that sparks are going to fly (the wrong way) when they meet each other for the first time, what more being coerced to work together on an impossible mission. <br /><br />Halfway through the Riyria Revelations I was already tempted to read The Crown Tower which fleshes out the back-story of how this legendary dynamic duo came together. Their banter and friendly bickering are so entertaining that I can only imagine how delightful it is to read their initial encounter when they despised each other. However, I was advised by a couple of experienced readers to finish Revelations first and I’m thankful for that. I’ve not read many prequels before and with hindsight I find that The Crown Tower is really more fun to read AFTER knowing what happened in Revelations.<br /><br />Firstly, I appreciated that we get a lot more of Hadrian and Royce, this being their introductory spiel after all. And as expected, reading their initial interaction was pure delight. They are still very much the Hadrian and Royce that we know and love, but each yet to be tempered by the other’s qualities, so to speak.<br /><br />Secondly, we finally have the backstory of Gwen, a truly admirable and strong woman who is also immensely likable. While she did not have much of an appearance in Revelations, her contribution to the overall plot was significant. In The Crown Tower, Gwen’s scenes provided a darker tone to the overarching story as we see how Medford House came to be. And of course, having read The Revelations, her tale brings a considerable amount of poignancy. <br /><br />Thirdly, the sly old fox, Arcadius. 'Nuff said save for the last couple of lines of the book; <br /><br /><i>"We've planted the seeds. All we can do now is wait and see what grows."</i><br /><br />While every reader who loved Riyria Revelations will most likely love this book, it also serves as a solid stand-alone which is testament to Michael J Sullivan’s writing and storytelling skills. A very entertaining read in a classic fantasy setting. <br /><br />And as a side note to Michael, you don’t ever have to worry about Hadrian and Royce overstaying their welcome. I just can’t get enough of them!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9847613479865052298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1135224777" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1135224777" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1135224777?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1135224777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5292643622754567561">The Crown Tower is the first book in the <i>The Riyria Chronicles</i> which is the prequel series to Michael J. Sullivan's highly entertaining <i>Riyria Revelations</i> series. The Crown Tower was just as good as any of the books in the <i>Riyria Revelations</i>. It was packed with all the action, adventure, intrigue, and the humor readers of the <i>Riyria Revelations</i> have come to expect from a book featuring Hadrain and Royce. <br/><br/>This was set 12 years before the start of the events told in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4345290.The_Crown_Conspiracy__The_Riyria_Revelations___1_' title='The Crown Conspiracy (The Riyria Revelations, #1) by Michael J. Sullivan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Crown Conspiracy</a>. It was th</span>
  <span id="freeText5292643622754567561" style="display:none">The Crown Tower is the first book in the <i>The Riyria Chronicles</i> which is the prequel series to Michael J. Sullivan's highly entertaining <i>Riyria Revelations</i> series. The Crown Tower was just as good as any of the books in the <i>Riyria Revelations</i>. It was packed with all the action, adventure, intrigue, and the humor readers of the <i>Riyria Revelations</i> have come to expect from a book featuring Hadrain and Royce. <br /><br />This was set 12 years before the start of the events told in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4345290.The_Crown_Conspiracy__The_Riyria_Revelations___1_" title="The Crown Conspiracy (The Riyria Revelations, #1) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crown Conspiracy</a>. It was the story of how Hadrian and Royce first met and became the team known as Riyria. Arcadius manages to manipulate both Royce and Hadrian into stealing a forbidden book from the Crown Tower, a church stronghold, for him. <br /><br />I loved the fact that Royce and Hadrian did not become instant friends. They grew to trust and like each other over the course of the story. Their banter was as hilarious as ever even when it was not so friendly. <br /><br />This book also added Gwen as a POV character. We learn a bit more about her gift and her life. All to good effect. I like her a lot better now that I know more about her. The story of her time in Medford was dark, but interesting.<br /><br />While this book was still a fun and exciting read, it was a little darker than the original series. Royce was just as wild in his early days as all those stories promised he would be and Gwen's own story was a bit bleak at times! <br /><br />Rating: 4.5 stars.<br /><br />Audio Note: Michael J. Sullivan made a sacrifice to retain the services of Tim Gerard Reynolds as narrator and it was worth it. Reynolds is the voice of Hadrian and Royce, for me. He was fantastic again in this one. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5292643622754567561" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/977063810?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee" href="/user/show/4162390-lee">Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4162390-lee?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer977063810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6595941485784222292">Ahhhhh Royce and Hadrian my old friends. Lovely to see you again. <br/><br/>I think it a testament to an author when characters become so loved that you become excited to be reading about them again. The first book in the Riyria Chronicles is an absolute gem and hearing all about how our two heroes met really feels like it is a story that should be told.<br/><br/>If you have read the Revelations series then this series (jumping the gun a bit here) is a must read. One of the things that I have enjoyed, apart from re</span>
  <span id="freeText6595941485784222292" style="display:none">Ahhhhh Royce and Hadrian my old friends. Lovely to see you again. <br /><br />I think it a testament to an author when characters become so loved that you become excited to be reading about them again. The first book in the Riyria Chronicles is an absolute gem and hearing all about how our two heroes met really feels like it is a story that should be told.<br /><br />If you have read the Revelations series then this series (jumping the gun a bit here) is a must read. One of the things that I have enjoyed, apart from reading about the two lads, is the patience and detail that Sullivan has added to the story to make sure that events that happen later are not just prefixed with a quick paragraph fix. I don't think that I am explaining myself very well. <br />It would have been easy for example to introduce somebody from future books and have them by chance meet another character and that is that. But Sullivan takes time to develop a story around the meeting that is very real and actually adds to your knowledge of the relationship. It is hard to image that this was written after the Revelations series because it is so historically detailed.<br /><br />That brings me to a interesting point. In what order should you read the series? In the intro, Sullivan explains that this could be a 12 book series. Each a stand alone and readable whenever, with an end point, so no cliff hangers. It allows him to write as many as he wants, or as he says, as we readers want. <br />The biggest problem I would have in reading some of this series before reading Revelations is the <s>writing</s> story quality. It took me at least 3 revelations books to become a fanboy and be hooked on the series. The first couple I scored 3 stars and thought they were 'ok'. The last few books are wonderful and once you are engaged in the Hadrian/Royce relationship. it is hard to put them down. Reading this book, the story and writing style is again superb. Book 2 of this series seems the same wonderful read. But if I was to now go to book 1 of Revelations I think I would be saying "wtf happened there? Is this the same author?".<br /><br />At the end of the day it is a moot point for me, as i have read the series, so I know how good it gets. But if anyone asks me what order to read them in. I am definitely recommending Revelations first, then the early years of Chronicals. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6595941485784222292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
