<div id="review_2277355468" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2277355468" />
    <a title="ChopinFC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51633786-chopinfc"><img alt="ChopinFC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545283749p2/51633786.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2277355468?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ChopinFC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ChopinFC" href="/user/show/51633786-chopinfc">ChopinFC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17278262-the-crown-tower">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2277355468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2606605699437678559"><b> full review...<br/><br/>What do you get when you join two completely different characters together: one and "assassin" and the other a soldier into a partnership? The answer is the 'Riyria Chronicles', a fast pace fantasy ,thrill-of-a-ride that kept revving up the engine into the very end! </b><br/><br/> I was really impressed with this first novel and to be honest wasn't quite sure the series was for me before I started it. After many recommendations from my GR friends to read the 'Riyria Revelations' I decided to sw</span>
  <span id="freeText2606605699437678559" style="display:none"><b> full review...<br><br>What do you get when you join two completely different characters together: one and "assassin" and the other a soldier into a partnership? The answer is the 'Riyria Chronicles', a fast pace fantasy ,thrill-of-a-ride that kept revving up the engine into the very end! </b><br><br> I was really impressed with this first novel and to be honest wasn't quite sure the series was for me before I started it. After many recommendations from my GR friends to read the 'Riyria Revelations' I decided to switch things around and actually start in chronological order and begin with the Chronicle series first. I didn't know what to expect, hell I didn't even know what the damn 'Riyria' Name meant! ( I guess it would help if I spoke Elvish which is exactly the meaning of <i>Riyria or partnership</i>)<br><br> My only other experience with Sullivan was reading Age of Myth and I enjoyed it a fair amount. In contrast, 'The Riyria Chronicles' is a complete departure from that work. The writing in Riyria is done exquisitely well, and Sullivan is very descriptive of different characters and the world surrounding our two protagonist Hadrian and Royce. There's a set order established in the book with certain linear chronology that really makes the story engaging. I've yet to read Riyria Revelations but I'm sure fans of that series have always wondered how both Royce and Hadrian have met each other. Sullivan does an awesome job of putting it all together in the context of the 'Crown Tower'. The story is super fast paced entertaining with loads of action. <br><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519070957i/25089157.jpg" width="400" height="385" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br> Ultimately what makes 'The Crown Tower' a real 'gem' is how the book blends two characters that are so polar opporsites, yet they complement each other beautifully! I guess Sullivan really want to prove the point that <b>opposites do indeed attract! </b><br><br> Hadrian is righteous in every way. He's an ex soldier with great brute power and amazing sword fighting skills. Despite his size and dexterity, he's gentle in nature and tend to believe in people despite their shortcomings. Royce on the other hand is a dirty scoundrel of an assassin, with a much smaller physique, yet he is extremely agile and cunning. Both dudes are almost like 'oil' and 'water', and despite their fundamental differences, we see them form a crazy and powerful union that will propel them into both 'Chronicle' and 'Revelation' series!<br><br> <b>Trust me friends when I tell you if you're into good fantasy, strong character development fun dialogue and great action, then Riyria Chronicles is right up your alley!<br><br>4 1/2 Stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2606605699437678559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer931556006" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17843548336812203592">Rating: 4.5/5<br/><br/>The Crown Tower is the first story of Hadrian and Royce. It's the story of how the met and decided to work together, even if reluctantly, for the first time in order to steal a book from... the Crown Tower. <br/><br/>This was the first Riyria book I've ever read and I am glad to say it did not disappoint. This book lives up to its hype. I loved pretty much everything. Especially the characters. The dynamic between Hadrian and Royce is what keeps this book alive. Those two are so different and</span>
  <span id="freeText17843548336812203592" style="display:none">Rating: 4.5/5<br /><br />The Crown Tower is the first story of Hadrian and Royce. It's the story of how the met and decided to work together, even if reluctantly, for the first time in order to steal a book from... the Crown Tower. <br /><br />This was the first Riyria book I've ever read and I am glad to say it did not disappoint. This book lives up to its hype. I loved pretty much everything. Especially the characters. The dynamic between Hadrian and Royce is what keeps this book alive. Those two are so different and can't stand each other. But when they actually manage to work together they were amazing. They reminded me so much of my best friend and I, my BFF being more like Royce and me being a lot like Hadrian. So, this book really hit home with me. <br /><br />I loved the action and humor it kept me reading until very late at night, or better yet, early in the morning. We also get to meet a lot more characters like Gwen, Arcadius and Pickles. Arcadius is kind of my personal favorite. I loved how you could never get a straight answer from him and how he manipulated Royce and Hadrian. I'm really looking forward to their next adventure and then I will be definitely picking up the Riyria Revelations books.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2143679373?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liam Degnan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liam Degnan" href="/user/show/8180038-liam-degnan">Liam Degnan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8180038-liam-degnan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2143679373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16198038877617419510"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Each killing steals a bit of humanity until a murderer is nothing more than an animal. A hunger replaces the spirit. A want for what was lost, but as with innocence, the soul can never be replaced."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><b>
  <u>3.5 Stars: ✰✰✰½</u>
</b><br/><br/>I was initially torn on whether or not I wanted to read the Riyria Chronicles, simply because <b>the Riyria Revelations had such a perfectly complete ending</b>. After waiting a few months, I saw the first two books on an Audible sale and figured I might as well pick them up, </span>
  <span id="freeText16198038877617419510" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Each killing steals a bit of humanity until a murderer is nothing more than an animal. A hunger replaces the spirit. A want for what was lost, but as with innocence, the soul can never be replaced."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><b>
  <u>3.5 Stars: ✰✰✰½</u>
</b><br /><br />I was initially torn on whether or not I wanted to read the Riyria Chronicles, simply because <b>the Riyria Revelations had such a perfectly complete ending</b>. After waiting a few months, I saw the first two books on an Audible sale and figured I might as well pick them up, because they seemed to be a good bit lighter than the books in the original series. <br /><br /><b>And I'm so glad that I did</b>. Hadrian and Royce as characters might be my favorite duo/bromance of all time, and this book only further solidified that for me. Sullivan does a seriously fantastic job of developing his characters in this book, even though plotlines might not exactly be his strongest point. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Character Development:</u>
</b><br /><br />I have said this with everything single book I have read by Michael Sullivan, and I'm going to keep saying it. <b>If you enjoy character-driven books and series, you will absolutely love these</b>. It's what keeps me coming back to his books, even though I definitely got off to a rocky start with Theft of Swords. <br /><br />These books take us deep back into the past of Hadrian and Royce (about 12 years before the beginning of Theft of Swords), and this specific book is the story of both their introduction as well as their first mission as a team. When you have two characters that are so completely different from each other as Hadrian and Royce are, it is hard to write about them becoming friends in a way that is believable. It quickly turns into a Hallmark kind of vibe if you aren't careful, which I hate with a passion. But Michael Sullivan's presentation of their personalities, the development of their relationship, and also their development as individuals <b>was accomplished as skillfully as anything I've come to expect from him</b>. <br /><br />An added bonus is that Gwen gets A LOT of page time in these books, which made me so happy. If you liked Gwen while reading Revelations, you will love this book. Sullivan is so excellent at writing strong female protagonists. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Story &amp; Plot:</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Now, here's the thing</b>. I can genuinely say that I enjoyed every minute of reading this book. It was definitely much lighter than the later books in Revelations, which I'm actually happy about, because sometimes I need just light reading. There weren't any huge plot holes or problems with the story, and it was entertaining. <br /><br /><b>But not a lot happened</b>. It felt a little too simple, which isn't a huge problem, but it lacked that "Wow" factor that I usually reserve for books that get more than four stars from me. Sullivan says that these books are more episodic in nature, as compared to Revelations (which had an overarching story throughout all six books that was being developed), and I'm hoping that means that we'll get some more interesting plots in the later books. <br /><br />Again, that doesn't mean I didn't enjoy this one, just that I found it lacking in substance as regards the story. <br /><br /><b>Some Final Thoughts:</b><br /><br /><b>This critique might seem a bit unusual</b>, because I didn't really see anybody bringing this up, and I felt kind of like it was worth saying something about. Basically a part of the story regarding Gwen (this really isn't a spoiler - it's mentioned in the first two chapters of this book AND Revelations), is that she is employed as a prostitute in an inn, by a guy who was very abusive and controlling. She gets out of this abusive and controlling relationship by leaving and opening a brothel of her own. <br /><br />And something about it just felt very off to me. For a young girl to be forced into prostitution out of necessity is just an awful thing, whether they do it by choice or whether they are pushed into it by somebody else. Regardless - it's a terrible thing. And everything about the way Sullivan wrote about this aspect of the story felt far, far too casual for me. Realistically, if we're talking about real life, I don't think that this is how it would have went down. And that made me take off another half star. If there's something I'm missing here, feel free to talk to me about it haha =].<br /><br /><b>
  <u>In Conclusion:</u>
</b><br /><br />If you enjoyed reading Revelations and you're ever looking for some light reading, I highly recommend you give this series (or, at least, this book) a shot. It adds a lot of valuable information and background for people who are fans of Royce and Hadrian, and the spotlight on Gwen did a great job of developing a character I wanted more from in Revelations. I say read it if you ever want "light reading", because the plot is definitely very simple, and you won't find anything in here that blows your might. But aside from my one personal issue, it's the kind of book that you can't help but enjoy =]. <br /><br />I'll be continuing with this series, for sure! <br /><br />(As a side note - I HIGHLY recommend reading through the entire Riyria Revelations series before you start on this one. Even though these are prequels, you will appreciate these books so much more if you have Revelations as a backdrop). <br /><br />Happy Reading =].</span>
  <a data-text-id="16198038877617419510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2123481927" />
    <a title="Phee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26480778-phee"><img alt="Phee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580467651p2/26480778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2123481927?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phee" href="/user/show/26480778-phee">Phee</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26480778-phee?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2123481927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6723511474416895422">Riyria, it’s elvish for two. <br/>And what a duo these men are. Some of you may know that I inhale read the Riyria Revelations series. It’s hard to read about Royce and Hadrian and not fall in love. Damn near impossible actually. I certainly did, and I knew I wouldn’t leave it long before jumping into Chronicles. I did actually try to start this one towards the end of October but I went to Japan then fell into a HUGE reading slump. Anyways, I picked this up again yesterday and what do you know. Inhal</span>
  <span id="freeText6723511474416895422" style="display:none">Riyria, it’s elvish for two. <br />And what a duo these men are. Some of you may know that I inhale read the Riyria Revelations series. It’s hard to read about Royce and Hadrian and not fall in love. Damn near impossible actually. I certainly did, and I knew I wouldn’t leave it long before jumping into Chronicles. I did actually try to start this one towards the end of October but I went to Japan then fell into a HUGE reading slump. Anyways, I picked this up again yesterday and what do you know. Inhale read. <br /><br />Sullivan’s writing has grown so much. It’s wonderful to see such a difference. Don’t get me wrong, the first Revelations books were good. But by the end they were excellent. The writing here is even better than in HoN. <br /><br />It’s so nice to return to this world and these wonderful characters. I’m so glad that Sullivan decided to write prequels and not sequels. The way he ended Revelations was so beautiful and perfect. Any sequel would have undone that magic. At the start of Revelations the duo are already well established as the wonder team, capable of pulling of impossible tasks. It’s so nice to see how they get started and to see the legendary heist of the Crown Tower. <br />I like that you could technically start with these books if you are new to the Riyria world. These Chronicles novels can be read before Revelations and each is a stand alone novel. But if you are new, then I would urge you to read the Revelations series first. It makes this all the more satisfying and as you know how it all comes to an end, you can just sit back and enjoy the journey when you get to these books. <br /><br />I love that we got to see more of Gwen’s backstory in this. I adore her, and I appreciate her all the more now. She is so strong and kicks ass in the best way. <br />I also really enjoyed the beginnings on Royce and Hadrian’s relationship. I say relationship because they really don’t get on at first. But as they say, opposites attract. <br />Also Royce was full of sass and eye rolls, gosh I love him. <br /><br />I’ll probably jump into the next one in the next few days. Being back with my boys has reignited the fire and thirst for more. I could read about Royce and Hadrian forever. </span>

<div id="review_1442197140" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1442197140" />
    <a title="Kristalia " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia"><img alt="Kristalia " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535637983p2/5705623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1442197140?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristalia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristalia " href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia">Kristalia </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Gentlemen Bastard</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=they-are-so-awesome-hot-and-stuff">they-are-so-awesome-hot-and-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=why-u-no-longer-u-make-me-sad">why-u-no-longer-u-make-me-sad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=be-my-heroes-please">be-my-heroes-please</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorites-absolute">favorites-absolute</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=be-my-heroine-please">be-my-heroine-please</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1442197140" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer526626814034555742"><b>Final rating: 5/5 stars</b><br/><b>Final rating - for the whole series: 5/5 stars</b><br/><blockquote>
  <i>The claw slipped again. It came off the edge of the stone and Hadrian felt his stomach rise as he fell. He dropped less than two stories and landed in a thick pile of straw, but it still hurt. With the wind knocked from him, he lay staring up at the sky and the wall.<br/>Royce’s shadow crossed his face. “That was pathetic.”<br/>“You’re enjoying this a little too much for me to think you’re honestly trying to help.”<br/>“Trust me. I want yo</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText526626814034555742" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 5/5 stars</b><br /><b>Final rating - for the whole series: 5/5 stars</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>The claw slipped again. It came off the edge of the stone and Hadrian felt his stomach rise as he fell. He dropped less than two stories and landed in a thick pile of straw, but it still hurt. With the wind knocked from him, he lay staring up at the sky and the wall.<br />Royce’s shadow crossed his face. “That was pathetic.”<br />“You’re enjoying this a little too much for me to think you’re honestly trying to help.”<br />“Trust me. I want you to improve. I want you to fall from much higher up.” </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />*review updated based on the whole series experience*<br /><br />After trying to decide for few days which order to read these books: chronologically - with this book as a start - or with publishing order (which is highly recommended by almost everyone) I decided to start chronologically. It's a choice that I do not regret, especially after finishing the whole series. And, given that I love to find out about characters as soon as possible, especially if it concerns their pasts, I decided to stick with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16043804.The_Crown_Tower__The_Riyria_Chronicles___1_" title="The Crown Tower (The Riyria Chronicles, #1) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Crown Tower</a> after reading few chapters of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10790290.Theft_of_Swords__The_Riyria_Revelations___1_" title="Theft of Swords (The Riyria Revelations, #1) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener"> Theft of Swords</a> - just so I could see what relationship the main characters have now. Even though author himself prefers the publication order, I just HAD to know how the main characters met and how they started working together. And this is how I began reading The Crown Tower.<br /><br />To be honest? I don't regret starting out this way - and this is how I continued reading them chronologically. When i read main series, i might reread the prequels (might include skipping a bit), especially all parts with Hadrian and Royce because they were so damn amazing and I loved them so much, with all their qualites.<br /><br />The two absolute main characters in this whole Riyria series are Hadrian and Royce - a mercenary and a thief-assassin. And this book is about their first meeting. (Given the first few chapters of the main series, they did progress... a little. Maybe a bit more). So, this is how they started out. <br /><br />This book was amazingly FUN, completely CAPTIVATING, and I READ it IN ONE DAY - this says a lot. I was even moved to tears near the end, it was really great. You know a book is great when you love the characters, love the story and definitely remember everything about it and characters as soon as you are done reading. When i don't like someone's writing style, I don't even remember sequence of events, even though that rarely happens. But this is one of the rare books where i remember ALL details. Thus a high rating - for enjoyment, memorability, fun and loveable characters.<br /><br />After finishing the whole series I have only to say: read. Read this series, you won't regret it. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11100431.Heir_of_Novron__The_Riyria_Revelations___3_" title="Heir of Novron (The Riyria Revelations, #3) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener"> Heir of Novron</a> is amazing conclusion and it was all well done. Even if these books are not the main series, I find them very important because you get to know the characters much better, which increases the emotional impact later on. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>► STORY:</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Sometimes your enemy can become your best friend. The one who will not betray you and help you when they should. And this is how it all began.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>After receiving news of his father's death, Hadrian </i>
</b>- a former soldier now mercenary - lost his way and purpose in life. Few years ago he had run away from his home because he wanted to become a knight in shining armor - but that proved to be only a dream when he realized he had become a killer instead. So he retired from army and started traveling the world. So, on his way to the man who knew details of his father's passing - Arcadius - he encounters a very intriguing boy nicknamed Pickles who offers himself as a guide and a mysterious hooded man who is followed by death. Hadrian gets on a river barge with 3 merchants, one mysterious lady (seemingly of high status), barge caretakers and the hooded man. And everyone is dead set on accusing the Hooded man as the murderer - there have been deaths in the city they just left and they all, except for Hadrian, believe that that particular mystery man is the very person who did them.<br /><br />⚠ <b>If you prefer to know less - skip the paragraph bellow and continue with the next one </b> ⚠<br /><br /> After a while, people around Hadrian start missing - until they are all gone, and he is the only one left alive by the most likely murderer - the Hooded man, who is nowhere to be found. Trying his best to report the murders to the city officer in next town - his effort was in vain, as he saw that not a single evidence remained. Continuing on to the University where Arcadius waits him, he finds himself reunited with the Hooded man - Royce. And Arcadius has a quest for them, which is a part of the last wish of Hadrian's father and a way to settle Royce's debt to Arcadius. They both accept eventually - Royce has to steal a book from a highest tower, but has to do it with the Hadrian's help, else his debt remains. After striking a bargain of his own, Hadrian agrees as well. <br /><br />⚠ <b>end of minor spoilers. </b> ⚠<br /><br /><b>
  <i>In the other town, Gwen, </i>
</b>a prostitute, decides to run away with the rest of the girls after one of the customers brutally kills their friend. Their boss didn't really care about the murder, he actually accepted the money for the "damage" and didn't ban the murderer. Gwen decides it's time to use a secret stash of money given to her in the past, and to run away with other women and make a place of their own. But time to do that must be right - both her and her late mother foresee the future - and Gwen's future is to help the man covered in blood who will come knocking on her door. And as the time passes, while struggling to make better lives for her and her friends, the signs start appearing... The man covered in blood will come soon.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>► CHARACTERS:</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />♘ <b>Hadrian </b> is a soldier without a purpose in life. Everything he wanted to do turned out to be just a impossible dream. So he begins traveling around and just... living. Hadrian is highly, and I mean highly naive - he is completely trustworthy of strangers - but he is also the type of the man who doesn't come after people if there is no evidence they are involved in something. Not to mention he is honest to a fault and he is really, really chatty person. He despises killing innocent people and is actually carefree person who actually does need a purpose in life. Hadrian is also a highly skilled warrior, as well as blacksmith apprentice - he uses the two swords he forged himself and one one handed big blade (not of his making). This allows him to switch styles whenever he wants and his technique is good - he just doesn't want to kill and involve innocents until proven otherwise. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Excuse me,” Hadrian said, and the man turned partway but not far enough to reveal features, not even a nose. After Sebastian’s comments Hadrian was curious about the man’s eyes. “My name is Hadrian Blackwater.”<br />“Congratulations.” The reply was as cold as the wind that carried it.<br />“Uh … what’s yours?”<br />The man turned away. “Leave me alone.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Even though he is completely naive, he is also honorable and really kind and good man who is just tired of senseless wars and killings. <br /><br />♜ <b>Royce</b> is a jaded, cynical man who lives his life completely isolated - he doesn't trust <u>anyone</u>. Given his unkind past and struggles to stay alive, he lives his whole life shrouded in darkness and doesn't allow anyone to get to close to him, especially not his complete opposite (Hadrian). Being in a huge debt to Arcadius, he must earn his freedom by doing what he is best at - thieving. But he is confused why Hadrian, who never stole anything like Royce had, is to be paired with him. And even more confused when Hadrian starts proving him wrong, even after Royce did everything he could to test Hadrian as much as possible; everything Royce believed (or rather, not believed) in comes crashing down around him and he starts understanding that people like Hadrian exist. He prefers isolation and loneliness to friendship and trust, he tries his best to drive people away from him, to make them angry at him so they would leave him alone. Cold and vicious and cruel, he has that tiny bit of humanity left in him... he just has a very hard time driving it out. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“I don’t agree with what you did,” Hadrian told him. “But thanks just the same.”<br />Royce shook his head. “You realize I’m just taking you to die.”<br />“I hope to disappoint you.”<br />“You won’t.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I thought Hadrian would be my fave, but I was proven otherwise. I found myself loving Royce as much as Hadrian, but maybe even more, given his actions later in the book. <br /><br />♛ <b>Gwen</b> is a strong and capable woman, who knows when to act, how to act and what to do. Keeping the promise to her mother alive, she does whatever she can to fulfill it. Her charisma and fast thinking saves the lives of women around her and she struggles as hard as she can to make their lives much better. Her capability to make friends of unlikely people just confirms how clever she is. <br /><br />Gwen was interesting and I enjoyed reading about her, but not as much as I enjoyed reading about Hadrian and Royce, but she was strong heroine and that is what matters.<br /><br />♛ <b>Pickles</b> is the teen who first robbed Hadrian of his purse, and then managed to convince Hadrian to let him be his guide to the town and to be his squire/servant while he is here. Pickles is highly adorkable and interesting. He is also very hyperactive and impulsive person. While there are not many scenes with him in the book, I liked reading about him. <br /><br />I will refrain writing about others as it would take a lot of time, but they were all interesting and I'm glad everything is settled and done by the time the book ends. I liked Dixon and Arcadius though, even though Arcadius was shady as hell. <br /><br />The first part of the book has Hadrian's POV, the second part has Royce's and Gwen's are between theirs and I was glad that they all had POVs.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>► OVERALL:</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />The only thing that threw me off was the sudden ending - I didn't wish for it to end there (it's not really a cliffhanger, but still), but the second book continues right after this one, so this is settled there. Reading the whole series was fun and interesting experience and I am glad I got to know characters before the main storyline. It made my experience much better.<br /><br />Overall, this was highly interesting book. I love the relationship between Hadrian/Royce. It was so well done.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>OTHER IMPORTANT INFO:</i>
</b><br />⚠ <b>Standalone:</b> Yes, but also no. Direct sequel is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17163514.The_Rose_and_the_Thorn__The_Riyria_Chronicles___2_" title="The Rose and the Thorn (The Riyria Chronicles, #2) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rose and the Thorn</a>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/110612-riyria" rel="nofollow noopener">Part of a series, </a>split in two parts: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16043804.The_Crown_Tower__The_Riyria_Chronicles___1_" title="The Crown Tower (The Riyria Chronicles, #1) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">Riyria Chronicles</a> (which happens before the main storyline, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10790290.Theft_of_Swords__The_Riyria_Revelations___1_" title="Theft of Swords (The Riyria Revelations, #1) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">Revelations</a> actual and completed main storyline. All of the books have beginning and ending, but are heavily dependent on each other. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16043804.The_Crown_Tower__The_Riyria_Chronicles___1_" title="The Crown Tower (The Riyria Chronicles, #1) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">Riyria Chronicles</a> can be read before or after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10790290.Theft_of_Swords__The_Riyria_Revelations___1_" title="Theft of Swords (The Riyria Revelations, #1) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">Revelations</a>, but I suggest Chronicles first as it is the beginning of everything. <br />⚠ <b>Point of View:</b> Third POV, 3 main characters + extras.<br />⚠ <b>Cliffhanger:</b> Somewhat? Actually, sudden ending, continues in the next book. <br />⚠ <b>Triggers:</b> prostitution and <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/FantasticRacism" rel="nofollow noopener">fantastic(fantasy) racism.</a>, and also <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ abuse of women, but those women get kick ass later and take no shit from others <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br />⚠ <b>Love triangle:</b> NO. THANK GOD.<br />⚠ <b>Angst:</b> Of course. But not always. <br />⚠ <b>Supernatural:</b> Yes. Elves, Dwarves, Gods.<br />⚠ <b>Mature content:</b> No. Mentioned, but nothing described.<br />⚠ <b>Ending type:</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[HEA  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />⚠ <b>Note:</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16043804.The_Crown_Tower__The_Riyria_Chronicles___1_" title="The Crown Tower (The Riyria Chronicles, #1) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">Riyria Chronicles</a> can be read before or after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10790290.Theft_of_Swords__The_Riyria_Revelations___1_" title="Theft of Swords (The Riyria Revelations, #1) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">Revelations</a>, but I suggest Chronicles first as it is the beginning of everything. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>► REVIEW(S) RELATED TO THIS BOOK:</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />◈ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1442197140" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Crown Tower (The Riyria Chronicles #1) </a> <br />◈ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1442197227" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Rose and the Thorn (The Riyria Chronicles, #2) </a> <br />◈ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1442199190" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Death of Dulgath (The Riyria Chronicles #3) </a> <br />◈ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1442196910" rel="nofollow noopener"> Theft of Swords (The Riyria Revelations, #1-2) </a> <br />◈ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1442196915" rel="nofollow noopener"> Rise of Empire (The Riyria Revelations, #3-4) </a> <br />◈ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1442196917" rel="nofollow noopener"> Heir of Novron (The Riyria Revelations, #5-6) </a> </span>

  <span id="freeText5404778601629248017" style="display:none">So far I've put every one of these on my favorites shelf. The story here goes back to the beginning of Riyria (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[in the book an elvish word. It means something like 2 working together as 1...sort of. I gather it doesn't translate directly <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>).<br /><br />Before I elaborate any more, I'll say I recommend this. It's an excellent read and a good addition to the epic fantasy genre.<br /><br />Now, in more detail. It's possible to start here with this volume (as it's labeled "Book 1") or to read the series first. As The author doesn't give a number of books he plans to write (which isn't a problem for me as long as they stay this good). He could I suppose write many, many adventures for Royce and Hadrian. (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The series comes at what is apparently the close of their career. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.) If you start with the series this will be an extended prequel filling in details of things you've already read about and telling stories of things we saw culminate in the said series.<br /><br />If you start here then a lot of the book will be foreshadowing and things will be said that are "pregnant" with possibility and portent (there are even oblique prophecies..."to be fulfilled later").<br /><br />Of course the only problem is that if you're like me you'll read this and run right out to get the series...then when other books come out, they'll be prequels.<br /><br />No big deal of course, the books are all good.<br /><br />So, recommended, enjoy. </span>

<div id="review_1389257179" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1389257179" />
    <a title="Marielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45124366-marielle"><img alt="Marielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572516394p2/45124366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1389257179?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marielle" href="/user/show/45124366-marielle">Marielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/28810646-the-crown-tower">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45124366-marielle?shelf=audiobooks-own">audiobooks-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1389257179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2060510588962876273">Loved reading about Royce and Hadrian getting to know each other! RTC</span>

<div id="review_2021439953" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2021439953" />
    <a title="Eric" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36502262-eric"><img alt="Eric" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501438390p2/36502262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2021439953?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eric" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eric" href="/user/show/36502262-eric">Eric</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36502262-eric?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2021439953" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1059645596996936999">3.5 Stars<br/><br/>The Crown Tower is a prequel of sorts to the Riyria Revelations series. We get to see how Hadrian Blackwater and Royce Melborn become the unlikeliest of partners. Anyone who loved The Riyria Revelations series will love the chance to see how the best bromance in the business first came to be. <br/><br/>The author includes a note stating that while Revelations was published first, the Riyria Chronicles (of which The Crown Tower is the first book) can be read either as standalone, read before Revel</span>
  <span id="freeText1059645596996936999" style="display:none">3.5 Stars<br /><br />The Crown Tower is a prequel of sorts to the Riyria Revelations series. We get to see how Hadrian Blackwater and Royce Melborn become the unlikeliest of partners. Anyone who loved The Riyria Revelations series will love the chance to see how the best bromance in the business first came to be. <br /><br />The author includes a note stating that while Revelations was published first, the Riyria Chronicles (of which The Crown Tower is the first book) can be read either as standalone, read before Revelations, or after. As someone who read Revelations first, I can definitely recommend reading the Revelations series before jumping in here. Events will make more sense and you’ll have greater insight into what’s happening. In fact, I would go as far to say that starting your Riyria reading experience with The Crown Tower may leave you frustrated. <br /><br />The first part of the book was quite slow. In fact, for a book that was under 400 pages, things didn’t really get going until nearly 300 pages in. Once things did pick up, the book ended strongly, leaving me wanting to read more about what happens next for Hadrian and Royce. The book seemed almost like an extended introduction setting up future adventures for the odd couple. <br /><br />While a bit slow, the book is well written and the strong conclusion showcased some of the fun banter and interaction that the Riyria stories are known for. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1059645596996936999" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_761982135" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/761982135" />
    <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan"><img alt="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553101944p2/4728718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/761982135?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan">Algernon (Darth Anyan)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer761982135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6700166443350001361"><br/>I read the book practically in one sitting, which says a lot about the talent of mr. Sullivan as a natural storyteller, making it seem so easy to get involved in the fate of his characters, sucking you in the adventure and making you read just one more page, just another chapter, just to see what comes next and how the heroes will get out of that tight corner. (It's true that my computer was also kaputt on Sunday and I didn't have the distraction of internet and social media to tempt me away fro</span>
  <span id="freeText6700166443350001361" style="display:none"><br />I read the book practically in one sitting, which says a lot about the talent of mr. Sullivan as a natural storyteller, making it seem so easy to get involved in the fate of his characters, sucking you in the adventure and making you read just one more page, just another chapter, just to see what comes next and how the heroes will get out of that tight corner. (It's true that my computer was also kaputt on Sunday and I didn't have the distraction of internet and social media to tempt me away from reading).<br /><br />I was already predisposed to enjoy the book, as I am a bit of a fanboy of the original Riyria Revelations books. The Crown Tower is a prequel to that, describing the first meeting between Hadrian Blackwater and Royce Melburn. A major part of the appeal of the series for me was the tight focus on individual characters rather than the big epic canvas with numerous rotating point-of-view characters and baroque political machinations - the same reason I liked the first two stories (the Crown Conspiracy and Avempartha) better than the last two (Wintertide and Percepliquis) with their more traditional big epic vibe. This prequel is also character driven and tight plotted, with the future buddy duo working hard at overcoming an instant dislike of each other in order to do a tricky heist job for their mentor - steal a precious book from the highest, most heavily guarded tower in all the land.<br /><br />The story was darker in tone than I expected, as both Hadrian and Royce are standing at a crossroads in their respective careers, coming from opposite directions: one too ready to trust in his fellow men and the other too cynical and self-centered. Separate they are broken and weak. Together they form a formidable machine. The time is not yet for friendly banter and leg pulling, as innocents and criminals alike are dying around the newly formed Riyria partnership, and the boys themselves do not escape unscathed from their first heist. But the best swords are forged and tempered through adversity and trust must be earned, not demanded.<br /><br />Hadrian, as the more trusting and with the kinder, more outgoing personality, is emerging better defined at the end of the volume than the secretive and taciturn Royce. We learn a lot about Hadrian's childhood in a small village, his training both as a blacksmith and as a warrior under his father's tutelage, his running away in search of fame and adventure, his disillusionment with the senseless killing that is the bread and butter of a soldier's life. About Royce we only find out that he grew up as a feral boy in the streets ('raised by wolves'), has been betrayed by his best friend and sent to prison, and that he believes killing is the easiest way to solve any problems he may encounter. The two impromptu thieves have still a long way to go before they forge their flawlessly functional dance at the edge of the precipice, but in the present book we are witnesses to the first step they take towards their destination.<br /><br />A third important thread in the book is about Gwen, another orphan that serves as a poster child for the abusive, demeaning manner women were subject to in medieval times. Beside the benefit of getting to know the origin story of yet another future character from Revelations, her storyline stands well on its own feet, like the girl herself who refuses to bow down before male violence, poverty and corruption. Gwen is also responsible for the single magical angle in the books so far (she has second sight).<br /><br />I have very few complaints : the plot is a bit predictable, there a some nice surprises and twists, but I felt mostly the book is about character development rather than the story of the heist itself. The prose is good, although there is a tendency to explain too much instead of letting the reader make his own mind, based on the deeds of the characters (some preaching to the choir, I felt)<br /><br />Conclusion : very good storytelling, a must for fans of the original series and a possible entry point for those yet unfamiliar with Royce and Hadrian.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6700166443350001361" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_422468896" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/422468896" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/422468896?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer422468896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17381608057489047846">The book is a prequel to Riyria Revelations. Basically it is a story of how Hadrian and Royce met and the reason they became known as Riyria (which means two in Elven). There were quite a few bits of information regarding early Riyria history in Riyria Revelations, so readers familiar with it will not find great surprises in the overall plot. The subplots are different matter though. <br/><br/>In the first chapter of the book Hadrian came back to civilized lands from south where he fought gladiator battle</span>
  <span id="freeText17381608057489047846" style="display:none">The book is a prequel to Riyria Revelations. Basically it is a story of how Hadrian and Royce met and the reason they became known as Riyria (which means two in Elven). There were quite a few bits of information regarding early Riyria history in Riyria Revelations, so readers familiar with it will not find great surprises in the overall plot. The subplots are different matter though. <br /><br />In the first chapter of the book Hadrian came back to civilized lands from south where he fought gladiator battles in the arena. He finally got fed up with this business, but he really has no clue what to do with his life anymore. The next chapter switches to Gwen whose POV makes up almost half of the book. <br /><br />The first thing I noticed about the book is that the beginning is much darker than the first book of the original series. The latter starts with established duo teaching highway robbers how to do their jobs properly; the former shows a gruesome murder of a prostitute (Gwen's chapter). The banter between Hadrian and Royce was half of the fun in the original series. Given that these guys officially meet way into the book, the banter is absent for quite some time. <br /><br />The original series evolves from some local jobs done by Riyria into a tale of epic quests, Empire-wide conspiracy, grand magic, and a search for a missing heir. This one does not have any epic feel; this is just a story of two completely different guys who also hate each other learning how to work together. <br /><br />I already mentioned that the beginning is kind of slow. Once the story finally gets rolling, it gets really exciting, I-do-not-need-no-sleep level of excitement. There are some very nice and unexpected plot twists along the way with the biggest one happening in the last chapter. <br /><br />The final rating for the book is solid 4 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17381608057489047846" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

	<tr>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('545RH2HVu6+iThwYuneIkySFmW/Jp76TrqoBmXBV+octkyQtHCQiQ6kn680dySjAI7alXNl7N8Yn0I3V479uuQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jXBTxDRTxBs3Xem3PUSvXNhNbqZP26y1XM7ihTWOGxxHbSb2SaJd9zw0HmKa+g8P335SlV8HJeDVtG7JpmSPIg==')})
  }
